Local News Two

Tens of Thousands of Obsolete Ming Calendars Confiscated

Superstitions and Spells Abound

Photos of Reactionary Figures Are Also Included

Japanese Are Also Privately Printing for Profit

Police Were Refused Entry Upon Investigation

After the National Government established its capital in Nanjing, it resolved to implement the Gregorian calendar and repeatedly issued orders to public security, education, and other bureaus in various provinces and cities, strictly prohibiting the circulation of the old calendar to emphasize the importance of timekeeping. However, general booksellers only seek profit and disregard the law. They take advantage of the concession areas where our country's police power does not extend to reprint these obsolete calendars and secretly sell them. Now that time flies, and the coming year is approaching, the bookstores and printing houses that are reprinting obsolete calendars are all starting their work. Director Yuan of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, in view of this, believes that if a large-scale investigation is carried out at this time, and once discovered, all copies are confiscated and destroyed, then obsolete calendars may not be seen among the people again next year. Therefore, he specially commissioned Inspector Ge Jingxuan of the bureau to investigate whether bookstores and printing houses in the city are secretly printing such materials. If found, they will be punished for propaganda of reaction, according to the central government's orders. In recent days, Inspector Ge has found four companies that are privately printing obsolete calendars: Tang Yunji Bookstore at No. 227 Siwen Lane, Datong Road; Zhang Peizhang Bookstore at No. 152 and 153 Nanchengdu Road; Huachang Printing House at No. 554 Beichengdu Road; and a certain printing house at No. 2093 Xingyu Lane, Haining Road. However, all of them are located in the Public Concession area. Therefore, at 3 p.m. the day before yesterday, he personally went to the Political Department of the General Police Station to request assistance in the search. The director of the department and Detective Pan Bi went to the Xinzha Police Station under their jurisdiction and dispatched detectives Zhang Jinlong, Yuan Xizhong, and Dong Xueyun to Tang Yunji, Zhang Peizhang, and Huachang. They saw that the obsolete calendars that had been printed were countless, both bound and unbound, numbering no less than hundreds of thousands. It would not be possible to transport them all back to the police station in a short time. They ordered their owners Tang A'gen, Wang Shaoshan, and Hua Wenbin not to move or hide the obsolete calendars and to await official disposal. They only took a small portion of the bound copies. The contents included all kinds of superstitious events, spells, and scriptures from the past, which were all published at the beginning. They were bizarre and can be said to be a collection of superstitions. The most absurd and outrageous thing was that the portraits of reactionary figures such as Yan Xishan, Feng Yuxiang, Li Bai and others were listed alongside the photos of the many officials of the National Government, which was tantamount to showing the public in an invisible way that the difference between right and wrong, and the boundary between the wise and the foolish, was indistinguishable. Then, they went to Xingyu Lane to search with detectives from the Huishi Police Station. Unexpectedly, the printing house was opened by the Japanese. They relied on extraterritorial rights as a talisman and refused the search. Although Detective Ge and others knew that the printing house had printed obsolete calendars, they were unable to exercise their powers and could do nothing. Yesterday morning, the police sent a portion of the obsolete calendars copied from the remaining three places to the Special District Local Court. Judge Shen of the Summary Court interrogated the search situation and ordered a change of date, awaiting a warrant to summon Tang A'gen and the other three to the court for further questioning, and ordered the police to search and send all the obsolete calendars printed by the three companies, Tang Yunji, etc., to the court for review.

Fires in Zhabei and Nanshi Claimed Human Lives

Zhabei... One Woman Died

Nanshi... One Girl Died

Xibao'an Road: A fire broke out at around 2:45 p.m. yesterday at the Xiexingli No. 82, Xinyi Spectacle Workshop, near the Yanjiage Vegetable Market on Xibao'an Road, Zhabei, and was extinguished at 5:30 p.m. When the fire was raging, Qiu Zhu's family, who lived at No. 82, was burned to death because they couldn't escape. A total of twelve houses, from No. 83 to No. 68, were affected. The biscuit factory at No. 83 and the Baofeng yarn factory were also included. When the fire trucks from the three sections of the fire brigade drove to the scene, they collided with the No. 4200 bus of the China Merchants Public Automobile Company at the intersection of Bao'an Road and Baoshan Road. Fortunately, the impact was not violent and there was no serious damage. However, according to the fire brigade's report, four firefighters, Kong Xianming, Shen Yunzhou, Wang Kaizhen, and Wang Kaibi, were injured in the chest, waist, hands, and feet. Qiu Zhu's family, who was burned to death, was from Yong. She was 45 years old and came to Shanghai a few days ago to visit her son-in-law, so she lived at No. 82.

Manufacturing Bureau Road: At 10:30 a.m. yesterday, a thatched shed in the second house near the Laojun Temple at No. 833 Lane, Manufacturing Bureau Road, Nanshi, was suddenly burned down. It is reported that the cause of the fire was because the place was very close to the railway. When the train passed by, a flame fell on the house, causing the fire. When the fire brigade drove to the scene, it had already spread to two houses (a total of three households). The second house was occupied by Yan Chengshun, who had given birth to a girl a month ago. Because the family was busy fighting the fire, the girl was burned to death. The fire lasted for 15 minutes and was extinguished at 10:45 a.m. Gao Changmiao, a patrol officer from the Second District General Office of the Public Security Bureau, personally supervised eight policemen to rush to suppress the fire and immediately brought Li Zhangshi (50 years old, Shandong native), the woman who started the fire, to the office for questioning. Then, he ordered the landlord to report to the court for inspection.

Mao Youfu's Rampant Lawlessness: Assaults His Mother, Violates His Daughter

Xie Jiao's mother and daughter were illegally detained by Mao.

They were tied up and severely beaten before managing to escape.

Show Ying's medical examination confirmed the violation.

Mao claims his wife was abducted and sold by the mother.

A woman from Yangzhou named Xie Jiao, along with her daughter Xiu Ying, resided in Yulin Lane, Pingliang Road. Xiu Ying, only fifteen years old, used to work at the Gonda Cotton Mill in Yangshupu. On the 28th of last month, at 6:00 PM after finishing work, she disappeared on her way home. Subsequently, a Mrs. Bai, who lived in the same house, informed Xie that Xiu Ying had been deceived and taken away by Mao Youfu, a resident of No. 88 Weixin Lane, from Zhenjiang. Mao's wife also worked at the Gonda Mill, which is how Mao knew Xiu Ying. After Xiu Ying arrived at Mao's home, Mao said to her, "Your mother has abducted and sold my wife. You must know the details. Tell me quickly." Xiu Ying didn't know what to say. Mao immediately grabbed a rope, tied her up, and beat her, hiding her in the front building. When Xie Jiao arrived at Mao's house, her daughter had just finished being beaten. Xie rebuked Mao for unreasonably bullying a young girl, but Mao retorted, accusing Xie of abducting and selling his wife. He then gathered several people, also bound Xie's hands, and dragged her into the kitchen, where they severely beat her with firewood. Afterward, he assigned an old woman to watch over her. Mao then moved Xiu Ying to the attic and forcibly raped her. Afterwards, he kept her confined in the front building, ordering his sister, Cai Mao, to watch over her. He originally intended to take her to the French Concession to hide, but the landlady of the second room, fearing future repercussions, strongly opposed it, so he did not proceed. Xie Jiao, trapped in the kitchen, could not cross the threshold nor call for help, so she had to spend the night there. The next morning, seeing the old woman watching over her still sound asleep, she immediately untied herself and escaped the trap. Waiting until the day before yesterday, she still hadn't seen her daughter return, and was forced to report to the Huishan Police Station, which dispatched Detective Cai Zhitian to Mao's house. They arrested Mao and his sister, Cai Mao, rescued Xiu Ying, and brought them back to the police station. Aside from detaining the siblings separately, they sent the girl to Guangren Hospital. After examination by a doctor, it was confirmed that she had indeed been raped. The doctor filled out a report and gave it to the police station. Yesterday morning, they summoned the victims, mother and daughter, and escorted Mao Youfu and Cai Mao to the Special District Local Court for trial. However, the old woman who was watching over Xie Jiao had already fled to an unknown location. The police lawyer, Li Zhishan, presented the case and submitted the doctor's examination report. Xie Jiao and her daughter Xiu Ying then recounted the details of being lured, beaten, and raped. When questioned, Mao Youfu confessed, "Because my wife was abducted and sold, I had the caterer's wife trick Xiu Ying into coming to my house. She claimed that my wife was abducted and sold to Pudong by her mother, and her mother also admitted it. Therefore, I confined them in my house, but they escaped and went to the police station to file a complaint, which was rejected. So I brought them back to my house. Later, the police station sent detectives to investigate, but I did not rape Xiu Ying," and so on. Cai Mao also confessed, "It was true that my sister-in-law was introduced and sold to a Mr. Yao in Laobaidu by Xie Jiao. I know nothing else about the matter." According to Cai Chen, Mao's landlady of the second room, Xiu Ying was brought by the caterer's wife. Mao slapped her cheek, but she didn't know whether he raped her or not. Judge Feng ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody and adjourned the hearing.

Three Leaders of the Notorious Bandit Tai Bao A Shu's Gang Arrested

Detectives confirmed their identities without error.

The three claimed to be rural farmers.

The notorious bandit Tai Bao A Shu and his gang have been harassing the townships and villages around the Su-Song area, committing rape, looting, and causing the people to suffer immensely. For several months, despite the dispatch of troops from Zhejiang and Jiangsu provinces to encircle and suppress them, the bandits' whereabouts remained elusive and uncertain. The troops would arrive and the bandits would flee, the troops would leave and the bandits would return, so that the banditry has not yet been eradicated. On the 27th of last month, a certain village in Jiaxing was again subjected to a major robbery. The Jiahe Bandit Suppression Commander dispatched troops to strike a heavy blow. The bandits were overwhelmed and scattered again. Pan Guifu, the self-proclaimed Deputy Commander of Tai Bao A Shu, led his band to flee to Qingpu. However, with the government troops pursuing them closely, and finding no refuge in the interior, he and key members Tang Songlin and Lu Yingen fled to the Shanghai International Settlement, awaiting an opportunity to act again. The Jiahe Bandit Suppression Command also anticipated that these men would flee to Shanghai after their defeat, so they dispatched Detective Chief Li Nianyuan and Detective Chen Xinde, along with informant Gu Agui, to Shanghai to investigate and arrest them. When the bandits rallied the masses to rob and kill at Baziqiao in Jinshan, Gu Agui personally experienced the robbery. Therefore, he recognized most of the key figures among the bandits, from Tai Bao A Shu downwards. The day before yesterday, he unexpectedly encountered the three bandits Pan, Tang, and Lu in front of the "Flower World" (entertainment area) on Nanjing Road. The location was only a stone's throw away from the Laozha Police Station. He immediately reported to the police, who dispatched Detective Song Bingzheng and Detective Cui Jinchuan to arrest Pan and the others. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Special District Local Court, where Judge Zhou presided over the interrogation. Detective Li brought informant Gu Agui to the court, who testified that Pan and the other two were indeed leaders of Tai Bao A Shu's bandit gang. When questioned, the three men denied everything, claiming to be rural farmers. In reality, these people gather to become bandits and disperse to become farmers. Unless someone recognizes them, it is impossible to discern their true identities. Judge Zhou stated that he could not immediately hand them over because the Jiahe Bandit Suppression Command had not sent an official document to the court. He ordered Pan and the other two men to be detained and adjourned the hearing for two weeks. Detective Li has now gone to Jiaxing to request the official document.

U.S. Consular Court Hears Garcia Case Yesterday

The Da Mei Evening News reports that the U.S. Consular Court held a hearing today (the 3rd) on the circumstances of the murder of Garcia, an American who had previously worked as a pilot at the New World entertainment complex, after he was killed at the intersection of Bazijiao Road and North Sichuan Road on Sunday morning (the 28th). The original coroner, Dr. Krillies, presided over the hearing. The first witness, a Mr. Fu who sold newspapers on Bazijiao Road, testified that he initially saw seven or eight foreigners standing at the intersection of North Sichuan Road and Bazijiao Road. A few minutes later, two rickshaws carrying two Westerners turned from North Sichuan Road onto Bazijiao Road, heading east. As the rickshaws turned, the foreigners standing at the intersection of North Sichuan Road began to hurl abuse at the Westerners in the rickshaws. These people were all Filipinos. Before long, the rickshaws stopped, and the two Westerners got out of the rickshaws. A scuffle ensued, and the foreigners scattered and fled. One person was bleeding heavily and was helped onto a rickshaw by his companion. He then fell from the rickshaw. The next witness, Western Detective Mei Sheng, testified that he was passing by Bazijiao Road at 4:15 that morning when he caught sight of Garcia and his companion, Frank. Frank seemed to be drunk, while Garcia had been stabbed and was bleeding profusely. He summoned two day constables to take them to Country Hospital, and he reported to the Hongkou Police Station. By the time he arrived at the scene, the Filipinos had already disappeared. Then, Dr. Pinnard from Country Hospital testified that Garcia died shortly after arriving at the hospital. An examination of his left chest revealed a knife wound, which was likely the cause of death due to excessive blood loss. Next, Western Detective Stock of the Hongkou Police Station testified that he arrested Filipino Spears at 8:30 on Sunday evening. Spears immediately confessed to the crime without denial. Finally, after testimony from Mrs. Taut, Garcia's employer, the hearing was adjourned to be continued tomorrow morning.

Fierce Battle Between Police and Bandits Outside Wusong Estuary

At around 9:00 PM the night before last, three large sailing junks suddenly appeared on the waters of Xingang Town outside the Wusong Estuary, carrying more than 50 pirates. They first robbed the merchant ships anchored in the harbor, then armed themselves and landed ashore, storming the town's Public Security Bureau and stealing more than ten rifles. Municipal Chamber of Commerce Requests Prohibition of Gangsters Intruding into Bookbinding Workshops

Teasing female workers and extorting male workers.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a report to the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday stating, "The bookbinding trade association claims that gangsters intrude into bookbinding workshops to tease female workers, and requests a strict prohibition. We are forwarding the situation for your review." The report stated that on October 2nd, the Shanghai Bookbinding Trade Association submitted a report stating, "We have instructed our members to open workshops, but gangsters frequently intrude, arbitrarily teasing the female workers.

They even lie on the worktables, making strange noises and acting wildly, which is unspeakable. As for the male workers, they make unfounded demands, and if their demands are not met, they start fights. The workshop owners hear about the gangsters but are afraid to intervene. This situation is particularly prevalent in the Zhabei district. If a strict prohibition is not issued, it will affect both public morals and business operations. Therefore, we request your association to forward this request to the Social Affairs and Public Safety Bureaus to jointly issue a public notice that, in the future, no one shall be allowed to enter the workshops without a legitimate reason or the permission of the workshop owner, to prevent disruption of work and unexpected events. Otherwise, the workshop owner shall be allowed to hand them over to the nearest Public Safety Bureau for punishment, in order to protect work and secure commerce." Upon investigation, it is a common practice for workshops in this city to employ female workers, and this is not unique to bookbinding workshops. Now it is reported that gangsters frequently intrude into the bookbinding workshops established by the members of the association, teasing female workers and making strange noises. They arbitrarily extort male workers, and if their demands are not met, they start fights. If such evil practices are not strictly prohibited, the impact will be immeasurable. We believe that it is reasonable to report the situation to your bureau for review and request that you send a letter to the Public Safety Bureau to jointly issue a public notice to strictly investigate and prohibit such actions, in order to maintain order in the workshops. This would be in the public interest.

Municipal Public Utilities Bureau Takes Over Streetlights in Fahua and Jiangwan

The streetlights in the Fahua and Jiangwan districts of this city have previously been managed by the respective district municipal committees. In order to unify authority and rectify the situation, the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau submitted a report to the Municipal Government, which was approved, and dispatched personnel to take over the streetlights separately on October 1st. This includes 24 kerosene streetlights in Fahua Town, 41 electric streetlights around Xujiahui, and 81 electric streetlights in Jiangwan Town. It is reported that the bureau will begin to reorganize the streetlights after the takeover, first replacing the older and less luminous electric lights with new ones, and then gradually adding new lights as needed. As soon as Fahua Town is connected to electricity, all the kerosene streetlights will be replaced with electric lights. Furthermore, since Jiangwan Town is far from the bureau's existing North Shanghai Streetlight Management Office, which makes management difficult, a Jiangwan Streetlight Management Office has been established in the town, which began operations on October 2nd. All streetlights within the district that were originally under the jurisdiction of the North Shanghai Management Office will be transferred to the Jiangwan Management Office for convenience.

Two Academic Societies Welcome Delegates to the World Power Conference

In May of this year, the World Power Conference held its second meeting in Berlin, Germany. The Chinese attendees included Mr. Huang Boqiao, representing the Chinese Institute of Engineers and the municipal governments of Shanghai, Nanjing, and Hankou; Mr. Li Yanshi and Mr. Shen Sifang, representing the Chinese Electrical Engineering Society; and Mr. Wang Shengsan, representing the Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Railways. All have returned to Shanghai one after another. The German, Austrian, and Swiss Alumni Association of the Chinese Institute of Engineers and the Chinese Electrical Engineering Society jointly held a welcome meeting at the Duyichu Sichuan Restaurant on Avenue Edward VII at 7:00 PM on October 1st. More than 70 members of the two societies attended and celebrated together, which greatly increased their interest. At the end of the meeting, Mr. Hu Shuhua delivered a welcome speech and invited Mr. Huang Boqiao and others to share their experiences and observations from their travels, so as to broaden their horizons. Mr. Huang then began to describe how European countries mostly establish themselves through industry. Currently, the world's sales are stagnant, causing 6 out of 10 factories to shut down. The number of unemployed people is increasing day by day. If this cannot be remedied, it may trigger unrest and affect global security. Even with the diligence of the German people, they still cannot avoid a difficult life. The Chinese people's food and lodging are too extravagant, and they should be frugal in order to save money for useful purposes and engage in beneficial businesses. Mr. Li Yanshi first described the excellent management of German factories. Unfortunately, the burden of war reparations has affected them, and their capital is depleted. They can only rely on borrowing American debt to facilitate circulation. Therefore, even though they are facing economic difficulties, they still have to maintain a grand facade in order to maintain international credit. Fortunately, factories and the government can help each other and still manage to maintain themselves. He then said that China's industry and commerce are restricted by unequal treaties. Taxes on foreign goods are lighter than those on domestic goods. Domestically, they are affected by the war, and public debt and treasury bonds are forced to be subscribed, causing factory operations to not be revitalized and capital to be exploited. He deeply hopes that the engineering community can provide sympathy and assistance to the industrial community, and that the government will reduce the burden on domestic goods manufacturers, so that business development and industrial prosperity can be expected. Mr. Shen Sifang said that the progress of the electrical industry in Europe and the United States is progressing by leaps and bounds, while the electrical industry in China is still in its infancy. Therefore, the Chinese Electrical Engineering Society was recently organized. In the future, he hopes that the Chinese Institute of Engineers and the German, Austrian, and Swiss Alumni Association will provide guidance at any time and cooperate fully in order to develop the future of the domestic electrical industry. The guests and hosts all enjoyed themselves and dispersed.

The Zhou Huchen Trademark Dispute: Wang Chunjian's Appeal Case to Be Announced

Wang Chunjian from Yangzhou leased the trademark of the Zhou Huchen brush shop from the Zhou Huchen brush shop in Jiangxi in the 16th year of the Republic of China (1927). He opened a brush shop on Xiangfen Lane in Shanghai, using the Zhou Huchen name on the brush handles, but adding the words "Zheng Ji" (Authentic Mark). However, since Shanghai already had the Zhou Huchen brush shop of Jin Yun, Fu Jin Yun, the owner of the old Zhou Huchen shop, filed a lawsuit in the Special District Court against Wang, claiming trademark infringement. Wang Chunjian voluntarily abandoned his rights and closed the shop, ending the dispute. Unexpectedly, Wang Chunhua, Wang Chunjian's younger brother, still had many unsold brushes with the Zhou Huchen name on them. Fu Jin Yun saw him in transit and took him to the police station. At the same time, Fu Jin Yun filed a complaint with the local court, sentencing Wang to two months in prison and a fine of one hundred yuan. Wang refused to accept the sentence and hired lawyer Jin Yu to file an appeal. The High Court ordered a retrial. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen opened a court hearing and summoned the police officer from Precinct 2, Section 1, He Shutang, as a key witness. After asking about his age and background, the judge asked how many words were engraved on the pen he found that day. The officer replied, "Only six words, 'Lao Hu Chen Yun Jin Zhi' (Old Tiger Chen Yun Jin Made)." The judge said, "That's strange. The pen name is engraved with 'Jiuchong Chunse Zui Xiantao' (Nine Layers of Spring Colors Intoxicate the Immortal Peach), and these seven words are larger than the six words below 'Lao Hu Chen Jin Yun Zhi' (Old Tiger Chen Jin Yun Made). The top seven words are colored blue, while the bottom six words are completely engraved but not colored. Instead, you clearly noticed the seven words 'Jiuchong Chunse Zui Xiantao', and only paid attention to the six words 'Lao Hu Chen Jin Yun Zhi'. And you also misspoke 'Yun Jin Zhi' (Cloud Brocade Made), it is 'Jin Yun Zhi' (Brocade Cloud Made). Were there any imitation calligraphy scrolls at that time?" The officer replied, "No." Then the appellant's lawyer, Jin, argued that the imitation calligraphy scrolls were wrapped outside the brushes. The police officer did not see them. How could he pay attention to the six words "Lao Hu Chen Jin Yun Zhi" which was not colored on the pen shaft, which is not logical. After much questioning and argument, the judge announced the end of the debate and ordered them to wait for the verdict on the 8th of this month and dismissed them.

Jianghai Customs Burns Opium Yesterday

Jianghai Customs held a burning of prohibited drugs confiscated within the 208th period at the steam kiln in Lujiazui, Pudong, yesterday. At 8:00 AM, Liang Qingyun, a committee member of the Customs Supervisory Office, went to the customs and, together with Ge Yixin, a representative of the Tax Affairs Department, and Robert, a Western warehouse manager, supervised Chinese and Western customs officers to escort the various drugs across the river to Pudong. Supervisors from various agencies arrived, including Liang Guang from the Garrison Headquarters, Yu Ding from the Shanghai Special District Court, Wang Zhizhong from the Local Court, Zhu Weiyao from the Municipal Government, Zhang Xingbang from the County Government, and Shen Chuan from the Anti-Drug Association. Zhang Mingqin, the district chief of the 3rd District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, led a platoon of armed police to the scene to maintain order. The burning began at 9:00 AM and ended at 11:00 AM. A total of 9 dan 21 jin 11 liang and 7.5 qian of opium were burned (estimated value of 95,004 silver dollars), as well as 17 iron barrels of morphine, weighing 4,072 liang (estimated value of more than 40,500 silver dollars), and 26 dan of poppy husks (estimated value of 390 silver dollars). In addition, there were 23 jin and 4 liang of pills containing morphine and 26 jin of anti-smoking pills (estimated total value of 1,014 silver dollars). Chongming Ship Capsizes in a Storm

All seven sailors and passengers fell into the water.

Fortunately, they were rescued by two Japanese ships.

The Chongming ship Jin Changshun set sail for Shanghai yesterday morning, loaded with horse manure. At 11:00 AM, when it arrived at the Kangtai sunken ship area of Sanjia Water outside the Wusong Estuary, it was suddenly hit by a violent storm, causing the entire ship to capsize immediately. The bottom of the ship faced the sky, and the three sailors and four passengers inside all fell into the water. Fortunately, Kiki Shoichiro, the head of the Tokyo Steamship Company residing on the Pudong shore who was salvaging the sunken ship Kangtai, saw it and immediately ordered the Jiangtai and Tongyi small ships to rush to the rescue. When the two ships arrived at the scene, they saw the drowning people clinging to the sinking ship. They rescued the seven people one by one and sailed back to the company's thatched shed. They ordered the people to disembark and change their wet clothes. Among them were Mrs. Huang, the 20-year-old wife of passenger Yin Dalang, and her 3-year-old son Zu Kang. Because they had been in the water for more than one minute, their faces were pale and they were unconscious. The Japanese personnel used hot soup to try to rescue them, and they gradually regained consciousness. Later, it was learned that Yin Dalang had brought his wife and children to Shanghai to seek employment, but all the clothes, bedding, money, etc. they had with them had been washed away. The public raised several dollars for Yin to use as travel expenses. The other crew members, Jin Zhangfu, Yu Hongbao, Gu Wanxing, and the other three, saw the sunken ship suddenly turned over by the tide, with the deck facing upwards. However, all the items inside the ship had sunk. The crew then took charge of the ship's hull and planned to return to Chongming for repairs.

A Sudden Assassin in the Birthday Hall

Li Deyuan Hosts a Feast for His Mother's Birthday

A Bloody Incident at the Huibinlou Restaurant

Li Deyuan, a 43-year-old Tianjin native currently residing on the upper floor of a rice shop in Rue Richelieu, French Concession, previously served as a patrol officer in the Second Precinct of the Fourth District of Zhabei. He has since resigned and started a business. Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, Li hosted a banquet for relatives and friends at the Huibinlou Restaurant on Third Avenue to celebrate his mother's 70th birthday. Unexpectedly, while Li was entertaining the guests, six men in short jackets appeared, claiming to be delivering gifts. One of them handed Li two silver dollars. As Li accepted the gift, unsure of who sent it, he inquired about the sender. Suddenly, one of the men stabbed Li in the buttocks with a knife, penetrating an inch deep. After withdrawing the knife, he attempted to stab Li in the throat. Fortunately, Li's friend, Wang Desan, noticed this and immediately stepped forward to block the attack. Wang's hand was also cut in the process, but Li was spared from further injury. Seeing that Li was stabbed, the six men, having achieved their goal, fled the scene. Li collapsed to the ground, bleeding profusely. Li's relatives and friends immediately gave chase, and two of the assassins were apprehended by patrol officers. Two daggers were confiscated and all were taken to the Xinzha Police Station, awaiting transfer to the Special District Court for questioning. The injured Li Deyuan was taken to the Beishi Hospital for treatment. It is said that Li's injuries are severe and his condition is critical. According to Li's wife, Chen Qiaoyun, the attack may have been carried out by enemies from her husband's time as a patrol officer in the Second Precinct of the Fourth District of Zhabei. Regardless, it was a tragic event.

Conspiracy to Rob a Bank Escort Foiled

Li A'da Loitered and Revealed Clues

Detective Team Arrested Suspects and Took Statements

Around 8:00 AM yesterday, four men, named A, B, C, and D, were seen near the Xinmatou Limmalu in Nanshi. One of them was wearing a military uniform, appearing as armed comrades. They lingered near the railway tracks, whispering to each other and looking around, seemingly engaged in a secret operation. Detective Xu Yulin of the First District, who happened to be passing by, found their behavior suspicious. The man in military uniform and another man were already gone, leaving only two men still loitering. They were immediately apprehended and taken in for questioning. One of them identified himself as Li A'da, a 30-year-old native of Chongming, residing in Lane 4 of Tianxiang Lane, Rue Paillet, French Concession. He confessed that his acquaintance, Lu A'xiao, a 27-year-old who worked as a chauffeur for He Dingfu, a runner for the Yi Shen Qian Zhuang at 88 Huayi Street, had told him that Yi Shen Qian Zhuang had been in business for many years and was very successful. Every morning between 8:00 and 9:00 AM, the bank would send employees to a certain bank with cash, usually around three to four thousand dollars, and that Xinmatou was a necessary passage for the escort. Lu said that if they were interested, they could wait there and easily obtain a large sum of money. Li admitted that he was tempted by this information and, along with his fellow villager Huang A'ming and the fugitive Li A'si, as well as Wu Yugen, who wore the military uniform, had conspired in a nearby teahouse to carry out the robbery today (yesterday). However, just as Li A'si had gone ahead with a handgun to commit the robbery, they were apprehended. Li also confessed that Li A'si was staying at a certain hotel. The other man identified himself as Huang A'ming, 36 years old, also admitting to the failed robbery. The detectives then went to the address and apprehended Wu Yugen, but Li A'si had already fled upon hearing the news. They also went to the Yi Shen Qian Zhuang and apprehended Lu A'xiao, who confessed to initiating the robbery plot. Wu confessed that he was 26 years old, a native of Taizhou, and a recruiting officer in the Training Regiment, also admitting to plotting to rob Yi Shen Qian Zhuang's money. As the case involved robbery, they were immediately transferred to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for questioning.

Worker Lin Xiyan Dies Tragically

Lin Xiyan, a 23-year-old Guangdong native and worker at the Asiatic Petroleum Company in Pudong, was moving Cylin yesterday morning at around 11:00 AM when a case suddenly exploded, striking Lin's head and burning his limbs. Extinguished This Morning

The flames quickly spread, engulfing the neighboring Huifeng Fish Shop at 15, the Taiyu Fruit Shop at 19, and the Changlong Vegetable Shop at 21. Chinese Managers of Foreign Firms Not Allowed to Join Chambers of Commerce

Joint Sino-Foreign Ventures Awaiting Central Government Approval

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter yesterday to the Copper, Iron, and Machinery Trade Association, stating that regarding the previous inquiry about whether Chinese managers of foreign machinery factories and Chinese managers of joint Sino-foreign machinery factories should be allowed to join the association as members, the matter had been referred to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for instructions. The Ministry has now issued a response, stating that pure foreign-owned companies and shops are not allowed to join chambers of commerce. Further, it has also quoted the directive from the Executive Yuan, stating that it is in conflict with the law. Regarding whether commercial legal entities or shops jointly owned by Chinese and foreigners can be allowed to join, the situation and opinions have been reported to the Executive Yuan for submission to the Central Government for approval, with instructions to be followed upon receiving the Yuan's order. Therefore, except for the issue of whether commercial legal entities or shops jointly owned by Chinese and foreigners can be allowed to join, which will be notified after receiving the order, this letter is to inform you for your reference.

Daily Economic Rescue

Free Talk

A Laughing Matter

— Sea Guest

Old Gentleman (sitting in a chair, pointing to his knee, to a child): Little friend, come over here. Would you like to ride on my knee?

Child: I don't want to. A fake mule is no fun. I'd rather pay money to ride a real mule.

Woman A: That scoundrel dared to insult me.

Woman B: How did he insult you?

Woman A: He talked to me at length about things during the Guangxu era, asking if I remembered them. Isn't that clearly insulting me, treating me like an old woman?

Company Manager: You're here to get a position, right?

Job Seeker: Yes, sir.

Company Manager: Do you have any certificates to prove your behavior and abilities?

Job Seeker: Yes, sir. I'm prepared.

Company Manager: Let me see them. Do they say good things?

Job Seeker: They couldn't be better, sir. Because I wrote them all myself.

A: Society is so hypocritical these days. Everyone is deceiving each other, making it impossible to trust even your closest friends.

B: What's even worse is that your closest friends can't trust you.

Record of Trivia at the North Station

— Lanxi

After a long period of preparation, the employees of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways have all received a badge. The badge is over two inches long and six or seven minutes wide. In the middle, there is a horizontal railway track, with a wheel with wings running on it. Of course, we know what this symbolizes. In the blank space above the badge, the words "Beijing-Shanghai, Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration" are written. The back of the badge is marked with a number, which has been properly assigned in advance. So-and-so's number is such-and-such. One gentleman received the number "606," and another received "914." Both looked worried and unhappy, but there was nothing they could do. "It's all predetermined," someone joked. "We have both internal and external medicines prepared here."

The autumn wind has swept across everything on the earth. We are now implementing an eight-hour work system, from 8:00 AM to 12:00 PM and from 2:00 PM to 6:00 PM. Director Liu is very serious about this. He inspects the offices early in the morning, limiting the hours that people come to the station. Every month, a new book is used for signing in. Everyone in our department is rushing to sign in the first two or three names. When it comes to the 13th, they all suffer from "Western superstition" and are a little embarrassed. No one wants to sign. They even say, "Mr. He Yingqin wouldn't sign on the 13th either." But no matter what, there is always a brave person who signs.

Train attendant Chen Yuting found 410 Japanese yen on the train, which was left behind by a Japanese lieutenant general. The attendant returned the money to his superiors without keeping any of it. Let's leave that aside for now. After discovering that his money was missing, the lieutenant general reported it to the Railway Department. The Railway Department found that the items lost by the lieutenant general matched those found by Chen Yuting and returned the money to the lieutenant general. The lieutenant general was grateful and thanked the Chinese for their old morality that had not been lost. He sent a letter to the Railway Department with 50 yuan, asking them to pass it on to Yuting to commend his righteousness and encourage others. The Railway Department refused, believing that this was the attendant's duty, and a major merit was sufficient. However, the lieutenant general sent the letter back, insisting that it was necessary. And so it was done, and Chen Yuting's reputation became very impressive.

Autumn Sounds on the Sea

— Xing Qiu

Cheng Yanqiu, a master of the Qingyi (lead female role) and Huashan (one who plays vivacious, coquettish women) styles, is unparalleled in his art, having established his own school. He is chivalrous, righteous, and respected as a virtuous man by the nation. This time, he is engaged by the Rong Ji Grand Theater, arriving in Shanghai for the ninth time to perform his best plays, fulfilling the expectations of Shanghai's audiences.

Yanqiu plays Zhang Yuzhen in "The Jade Bracelet." Amidst the splendor, he embodies the four virtues of "seclusion, gracefulness, chastity, and tranquility." The various imaginings in the wedding night scene are like unraveling silk from a cocoon, with layers of emotions unfolding. His expressions of surprise, shyness, resentment, and affection change in an instant. His forbearance before his aunt, his concealment before his mother, his veiled anger before his husband, and his dignified demeanor before his maidservant are all perfectly rendered. He is truly a master of emotional expression. His singing is equally impressive: the Xipi tune before dressing up, the Nan Bangzi in the wedding chamber, the Erliu when bidding farewell to his mother, and the Erhuang in the sickroom are all refined through countless practice sessions, exquisitely showcasing the nuances of lingering emotions, entanglements, pauses, and sobs. The softness and trills of his voice, and the novelty of his melodies, are simply breathtaking.

"The Fa Men Temple" is an extremely old, difficult, and valuable Qingyi Zheng Gong (pure and proper lead female role) play. Yanqiu has a natural gift for singing, so understanding the melodies is easy. He also comprehends the essence of the performance. Therefore, performing this play, he turns difficulties into ease, achieving perfection effortlessly. Further complemented by Wang Shaolou as Zhao Lian and Jin Shaoshan as Liu Jin, their performances are even better as the trial progresses. Jiang Miaoxiang, Furong Cao, Wu Fuqin, and Wen Liangchen each excel in their respective roles.

Yanqiu, standing tall and graceful, is particularly elegant in Qing dynasty attire. His performance of the "Visiting Mother" and "Returning the Order" scene, from singing to acting to recitation, is flawlessly brilliant. The questions and answers in the scene are especially fitting, and the detailed performance is unprecedented. The subtlety in the oath, the gracefulness in the curtsy, and the agility in stealing the order are all exquisitely portrayed. Zhundai's demeanor of shock and helplessness while returning the order is like mercury spilling onto the ground, penetrating every crevice. The way he gives his greetings are graceful, unhurried, and unafraid. The singing in Yaoban, Daoban, Kuaiban, and Manban are all clear in pronunciation, novel in melody, and exquisite in tune.

In Yanqiu's "Fen He Bay," the singing is clear in pronunciation and exquisite in every tune. The acting is vivid and lifelike. In the scene where she instructs Ding Shan, the dialogue is subtle and the movements are composed, perfectly capturing the loving heart of a mother. In the "Trouble at the Kiln" scene, the vanity of a woman and her fit of pique are portrayed with exceptional realism. Yanqiu, feeling that it was not beautiful enough, expanded the story into a full-length "Liu Yingchun," starting from Liu Yuewai building a house and Xue Rengui begging for money, all the way to "Fen He Bay," for a total of twenty-four scenes. There are literary and martial elements, singing and acting, reunions and separations, joys and sorrows, riches and poverty, encompassing the grand panorama of human affairs. It is a masterpiece that is appreciated by both the refined and the common.

A Strange Tale of Cursed Grass

— Jing Mengdie

In the border regions of Yunnan, there is a custom of "cursing grass," using human effort to create a magical entity. This is done during a young woman's maidenhood. In the years before marriage, to ensure future control over her husband, she selects a grass outside the wall in the garden and curses it. The method is as follows: every morning, she walks alone to the grass, first breathing on it three times. Then, she whispers to it, "I love you... Can you listen to me?... Can you do as I wish?" This is done every morning, becoming a daily ritual, rain or shine, for three years. The grass will then remain green throughout the year and become spiritually connected to her. When the woman smiles at it, the grass will stretch its branches and leaves, showing joy. If she shouts at it sternly, it will shrink its leaves and lower its head, showing fear. At this point, the woman happily tells her mother that the cursing of the grass is successful. The mother then accompanies her daughter to the grass to test it. If it works as expected, she is also surprised and delighted. She then plucks the grass and brings it home to make into a medicine, which she keeps secret as a gift for her daughter's wedding. This custom has been practiced for a long time, passed down from mother to daughter. The woman brings this medicine to her husband's home and secretly places it in his food for the groom to eat. Her husband will then, without realizing it, develop a mixture of love and fear toward his wife, paying close attention to her expressions and serving her with care. He will share her sorrows and joys. He will become so docile that he will obey her every command, kneeling when told and rising when permitted. Even if she whips him, he will bear it without complaint. Even the most brutal of ancient punishments would not be as harsh as this. The limits of incense and water are not as strict as this. This was recounted by a friend who was a government official in Yunnan. Men grow protective grass to forget their sorrows, find joy in seeing mimosa trees, nurture brotherly love with the purple Bauhinia, and stir thoughts of longing with red bean branches. Plants that are spiritually connected often respond to human emotions, but none are as strange and bizarre as this. Perhaps, among uncivilized barbarians, unusual customs develop. Through the binding of sincerity, even metal and stone can be opened. Or perhaps, reason dictates that this should be so.

An Amusing Anecdote Amidst Bandit Suppression

— Gong Yu

A guest spoke of an amusing incident during the suppression of bandits in Lindong Township. Due to years of flooding in Linhai, the local area was extremely desolate. Those with some assets could barely survive, but the extremely poor mostly became bandits, leading to a surge in banditry that was extremely harmful. Government troops were sent to suppress them, but the bandits would simply flee elsewhere, making it difficult to eradicate them completely. In addition to ordering the people of each village to defend themselves, the county government also set rewards, encouraging people to capture bandits: a certain amount for capturing them alive, and a certain amount for killing them. As a result, the people were extremely active. Whenever bandits attacked or government troops advanced, they would bravely assist. Soldiers who captured or killed bandits were also rewarded according to the regulations. Previously, Yang Chuanxi's gang of bandits had sent letters to the villages of Tantou and Chishui, demanding 1,000 yuan. The villages ignored them and secretly reported to the garrison in Dongcheng Town. A platoon of provincial security guards was stationed there, led by Platoon Leader Hou. After learning that Yang and his gang would attack on a certain morning, Hou led his twenty-odd men and ambushed them on the side of the road. When Yang's gang arrived, they suddenly attacked, leading to a fierce battle. At first, Hou's forces were at a disadvantage due to being outnumbered. But then, the villagers of both villages beat gongs and gathered to assist the government troops, and the nearby anti-smuggling patrol also rushed to the scene upon hearing the news, quickly gaining the upper hand. Yang's gang could not resist and retreated. One of the soldiers from the anti-smuggling patrol saw a bandit fall to the ground after being shot. Thinking he had killed the bandit, he ran to the bandit to cut off his head and claim the reward from the county government. Unexpectedly, this bandit, though fallen, was not dead and still had a handgun. When the soldier approached, the bandit fired a shot, hitting the soldier's wrist. The soldier was in extreme pain and nearly fell. At the same time, another soldier ran over. The bandit fired again, but missed, and had used all of his bullets. The soldier, however, had a gun and bullets, and shot the bandit dead. The soldier with the injured wrist endured the pain and cut off the bandit's head. Enraged that the bandit had injured his wrist, he dug out the bandit's eyes, ears, nose, and mouth with his bayonet, leaving the head a bloody mess, barely recognizable as human. After the remaining bandits dispersed, the soldier carried the head to Hou, asking him to report it to the county government so he could receive the fifteen-yuan reward as per the regulations. Hou, seeing that the eyes, ears, nose, and mouth had all been dug out, felt that it was too cruel and was displeased. He simply handed the soldier a few cigarettes, saying, "Go, go. This is a small reward for your service in killing the bandit. But in the future, be careful not to do this again. There is no such method of punishing bandits in the world." Thus, because of his momentary anger, the soldier lost both the fifteen-yuan reward and the right to it, along with the bandit's eyes, ears, nose, and mouth. He only received a few cigarettes, and couldn't help but lament his misfortune.

The Life of Mr. Zhao Tieqiao (1)

— Zhao Guangzu

On July 24th of the 19th year of the Republic [1930], bandits assassinated my late father next to the side gate of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's General Administration in Shanghai. Guangzu received the telegram and rushed to mourn him. I had only been in Paris for a few days, having left the country only fifty days earlier. I still remember when I left, my late father told me, "My son, you are now grown up and should be sensible. It is not easy to study in Europe. Our family has no accumulated wealth. Everything I earn through hard work while I am still healthy will be given to you. If that is not enough, I will borrow to help you. But I am a party member, and this body is not mine. If I am unfortunate, I entrust your mother and younger siblings to you." Guangzu understood the pain in his words, thinking that academic success would bring him comfort. Who knew that only fifty days after leaving the country, I would become a fatherless person, and my mother and siblings would weep blood thinking of these words.

My late father had been in charge of the bureau for over two years, arriving at the bureau every day at 9 AM. He would normally enter through the Bund's main gate. That day, at 8:30 AM, my mother and late father were riding together, passing the side gate on Fuzhou Road. An attendant helped my late father alight. He entered the gate, climbed a few stone steps, and before he could reach the top, a gunshot rang out. The attendant fell to the ground to avoid the bullet. Another shot rang out, and my late father was wounded and ran quickly upstairs, sitting in the secretary's office. His inner and outer garments were completely red. The assassin fled through the gate. My mother saw it from the car and called for the police. The driver also honked the horn, but no one responded. In a hurry, my late father drove himself to Baolong Hospital. Before arriving, he changed to the Red Cross Hospital. The hospital doctor performed surgery, removing several bowls of contaminated blood. Upon examination, one bullet had entered from the back, damaging the liver, and exited through the right abdomen. Blood flowed out uncontrollably. In the afternoon, the pain intensified. He died at 9 PM. Attempts to capture the assassin were unsuccessful. However, acquaintances and strangers alike said that my late father had died for the sake of the bureau's affairs.

In October of the 16th year [1927], my late father took office as the Director-General of the Supervisory Office of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. In February of the 17th year [1928], the bureau was reorganized, and he also served as the Director-General of the General Administration. In June of the 18th year [1929], the National Government specially appointed a commissioner to be responsible for the restructuring of the bureau, with the Director-General acting on behalf of the commissioner. The bureau had been established for over fifty years. The inadequacies in regulations, the poor organization, the unclear system, the source of embezzled funds, and the nests of corruption and laziness were rampant. Once someone entered its ranks, their siblings, wives, and concubines, as well as their impoverished acquaintances and even the impoverished acquaintances of their siblings, wives, and concubines, would all depend on it for food and clothing or seek great profits. After the fall of the Qing dynasty, the problems became even worse. From Yuan Shikai, Xu Shichang, Cao Kun, and others, high officials were successively appointed to take over, but those appointed were afraid of trouble and greedy for profit. They brought gold with them but left without ever taking office. After the National Government organized a committee to investigate and restructure it, the task of reform was entrusted to my late father. Some advised my late father not to enter the bureau in the name of the government, and that hundreds of thousands of yuan could be obtained quickly. My late father was unmoved. Then they plotted to intercept and coerce him, but he still refused to yield. Then they plotted to slander him. My late father entered the bureau, proclaimed the government's intentions, changed the accounting system and the organization of the bureau, reorganized the business, created detailed statistics, established regulations, set budgets, saved on materials, managed the wharves, and cleared the bureau's assets. There was nothing, no matter how big or small, difficult or easy, that he did not handle, to promote benefits and eliminate harm. There was no private collusion above or below, and no suspicion inside or outside. Ten months after the reorganization, business revenue increased dramatically, silencing and silencing those who plotted to slander him. He had drafted a fundamental reform plan for the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, advocating for "commercial enterprises to be state-run." Before the proposal could be finalized, the country was beset by many troubles. Most of the bureau's coastal ships were requisitioned for military use. The business had recovered but declined again. My late father died with grievances unaddressed.

Warmth in My Heart (287)

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 14: Tears on the Bamboo, a Broken-hearted Beauty; The Scent of the Lotus Fades, a Young Woman's Soul Departs

Cuiyun thinks about her current situation, which is even more distressing and less free than being a courtesan in a brothel. In a brothel, there are still people who pity her, people who might rescue her, and she can still think of ways to redeem herself. Now, she has no relatives or friends to turn to. Her body is forever sold to them, with no chance of turning her life around. Is this how her life will end? Living such a life is worse than death. She feels like a critically ill patient in a hospital with no hope of recovery, waiting only to die. Even if she dies, no one will know. She will simply be moved out. Feeling that there is no hope for the future, she can't muster any enthusiasm for anything. Young women naturally love to dress up, but she has no interest in dressing up anymore. As her body completely weakens, she resolutely loses the desire to even roll cigarettes. She claims she is sick and cannot get out of bed. The Ningbo old man has to ask others to roll cigarettes for her. He mutters to himself, "Even pigs that are slaughtered aren't eaten with their hair on. If you don't roll cigarettes, am I supposed to die from withdrawal?" But pretending to be sick can lead to real illness. At first, Cuiyun was simply unhappy and lacked energy, so she stubbornly stayed in bed, unwilling to roll cigarettes for him. Later, she suddenly started coughing, thinking she might have caught a cold. She didn't pay much attention. But then, she started coughing up phlegm with some blood in it, and there was a bloody taste in her throat. She quickly looked into the spittoon and felt her heart pounding and her body half-numb. She thought to herself, "It's over. This is the end." As she carefully examined the spittoon, a little maid in the house rushed to tell the Ningbo old man that the concubine was spitting blood. The Ningbo old man said, "Why are you making such a fuss? You don't even know if it's blood from her teeth or her lips. Blood always puts on such airs!" Cuiyun initially tried to comfort herself, thinking that it might not be blood from her lungs and that her heart was pounding because she was frightened. But after a moment, the fine, annoying strands of blood were still mixed in, and she felt an itch in her throat, making her want to cough. After coughing, she wanted to spit, and her phlegm always had strands of red in it. At that time, Zhang Yiqing had gone to Hankou again. Cuiyun took a long breath and couldn't help but shed tears. She thought, "At first, I thought I was like a hopeless patient in a hospital. But I wasn't actually sick then. Now I really am sick!" That night, her pillow was soaked with tears. A few days later, Zhang Yiqing returned. She told him about it, and he was a bit startled. But when he looked at Cuiyun, with her yellow, emaciated face and large, sunken eyes, she looked completely like a patient. He felt that leaving the fun and exciting places to keep company with a patient diminished the enjoyment. Therefore, he couldn't help but feel a sense of disappointment towards Cuiyun.

This Month's Flour Fell by Three "分"

Yesterday's flour market, after opening in the morning, the May market was initially stable. However, after the second round, this month's market suddenly fluctuated. Because most of the large number of warehouse receipts from the previous month had not been cleared by the bulls, the goods from those receipts were the accumulated goods when they were new flour. After several months of storage, the quality of the flour was inevitably slightly changed. Therefore, the customers generally did not care about selling those warehouse receipts, which made the large households inevitably panic. Therefore, they sold a large amount of the standards for this month to avoid further loss. The factories with goods were still continuously clearing their positions, because the higher the price, the more chances they had to dump. Therefore, this month's market fell sharply step by step. A certain factory also stopped maintaining and secretly dumped wildly, so the market was very weak and fell into the 4 "錢" mark. If there is no way out for this market, the bulls will inevitably suffer losses. As a result, this month's market fell by 3 "分" compared to the previous day, November's market fell by 1 "分" and 7.5 "厘", December's market fell by 1 "分", and March's market fell by 1.5 "分" and 1.75 "厘".

Wheat Futures Market Unanimously Downstream

Yesterday's wheat futures market, after opening in the morning, because the foreign wheat price was still good by about 4 "角", people's hearts were once excited. However, later, because the flour price was not good, and those who had already established short positions in foreign wheat saw this high price and dumped wildly again, the market appeared to be weak again. In the afternoon, it was reported that the flour market would collapse because the customer sales were not good. As a result, the selling pressure for each month became very smooth, and the market also fell sharply step by step. This kind of non-constant reversal is because people's hearts have gone astray and it is difficult to grasp. As a result, this month's market fell by 7 "分" compared to the previous day, November's market fell by 8 "分", December's market fell by 4 "分", February's market fell by 6 "分", and March's market fell by 5 "分". The current wheat market, because the factory demand is still good, the various "當" had ups and downs. The medium and next grade goods will eventually be killed. 13,000 bags of Shandong Hongri wheat, Haizhou Daoren, Qiao Dongtai, and Yao Wan resident horse shop wheat were all handled by Fuxin.

Yesterday, Dalian Yuan soybeans, because the Lian market reported upward again for December term, various parties entered actively and smoothly. The closing price was 4 taels and 9 "錢" and 2 "分", which was 4 "分" better than the previous day.

Silk and Tea: Milan Italian Cocoon Price Falls Again

The various silks in the Milan market are because the European sales of Italian silk are trending towards stagnation, the stock of silk is increasing day by day, most of the factories are reducing labor and stopping the machines, and the sales of dry cocoon factories are even more lifeless. The cocoon price is falling step by step. Last week, the spring dry cocoon was only 84 lira, the summer cocoon was 76 lira, and the autumn cocoon was 61 lira, falling another 1-2 lira. The trend is still difficult to stand up.

Foreign Firm Silk Sales Increasingly Sparse

Yesterday's foreign firm silk market in Shanghai became increasingly sparse, because all the silk factories in Shanghai had announced that they had stopped business, the factory silk had no market, and the telegrams for European and American silk were still not turning to Shanghai. The European firms' purchase demand was increasingly quiet. Yesterday, only Xinfu and others took in 30 packages of Sichuan yellow raw silk, and Boxing and others took in 11 packages of yellow raw silk. The prices were generally flat and weak.

The black tea market is even more stagnant, and there is no news of the British and Russian firms moving.

Jin Xing Necktie Company on Fifth Road and Shilu West announces that it has established a manufacturing plant at No. 422 Baoshan Road, Zhabei, on a grand scale, making it the leader in the necktie industry. The grand opening will be on the 1st, and a major sale will be held for seven days starting on the 2nd. Bow ties and neckties will start from 25 cents each, and shirts will start from 95 cents each. There will also be free gifts. This is a genuine sacrifice, not a long-term sale designed to deceive people.

Guanghua Bookstore on Fourth Road announces that its low-price promotion period has already ended. However, it is now the start of the school season, and the number of readers will not decrease. To save money, the promotion period will be extended for another half month. Local editions are 20% off, and foreign editions are 10% off. The special used book sale section attached to the store welcomes people to browse and purchase.

Sichuan Store announces that silver ear fungus, also known as white fungus, is known to all as a supreme tonic. However, the specific benefits are not well understood. Recently, this store in Paobujiao has used its many years of sales experience and its experience visiting the place of origin to write a silver ear fungus guide. The guide details the benefits, dosage, identification, and production conditions of silver ear fungus, allowing buyers to have a reference. This is truly well-intentioned and thoughtful. Those who bring Shen Bao to request this book will receive it as a gift from the store.

Theater News

The Paris Grand Theater announces that it will begin showing the Wufa Company's epic film "The History of the Barber" today. The film stars Werner Krauss, a male star comparable to Emil Jannings, and the beautiful and talented female star Jenny Jugo. It tells the story of a performer's love affair. The plot is full of twists and turns, with humorous and lively interludes, truly resembling "The Four Heavenly Kings" in its uniqueness. This is a rare silent epic film of modern times. In addition, the Montmartre Dance Troupe has been specially retained to perform on stage for one day as a farewell tribute.

The Mingxing Film Company announces that the Minzhong National Sound Film Company's first domestic sound film, "Songstress Red Peony," after months of preparation and careful design, began filming at the beginning of last month by the producer, our company. Filming has been proceeding day and night, and half of the film is now complete. It is expected to be completed in the shortest possible time, bringing this all-singing, all-dancing, all-dialogue domestic sound film to domestic and foreign audiences who have been longing for it for a long time. The main character, the songstress Red Peony, is played by the famous actress Hu Die. The other supporting actors are all well-known.

The Zhongshan Grand Theater announces that the Mingxing film "A Red Egg," which began showing yesterday, is, as the name suggests, a social comedy. However, upon seeing its content, it is actually a touching tragedy. The performance is so realistic that it feels like it actually happened. Viewers can understand the emotions and identify with the characters throughout. Zhou Wenshu plays a middle-aged woman, and her every move exudes the demeanor of a virtuous mother in an old family. The makeup is excellent, surpassing all others. The theater was almost full yesterday, both day and night. The 2,000 red eggs prepared will continue to be given away today.

The Wanguo Film Company announces that since its internal reorganization, its performance has been remarkable. Investors have been very enthusiastic, the capital is sufficient, and the scope has been greatly expanded. The film "Night of Terror," which is mostly completed, has been rushed to completion recently. The second production, "Hero," a martial arts fantasy film with gadgets written by the playwright Li Changjian, has been completed and is now being equipped with special costumes and props and can be filmed soon.
